Peaks</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hay%E2%80%93Herbert_Treaty" title="Hay–Herbert Treaty">Hay–Herbert Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> A larger-than-life <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_James_Cook,_Hyde_Park" title="Statue of James Cook, Hyde Park">statue</a> of Cook upon a column stands in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Sydney" title="Hyde Park, Sydney">Hyde Park</a> located in the centre of Sydney. A large aquatic monument is planned for Cook's landing place at <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a>, Sydney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the earliest monuments to Cook in the United Kingdom is located at <a href="/wiki/The_Vache" title="The Vache">The Vache</a>, erected in 1780 by Admiral <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Palliser" title="Hugh Palliser">Hugh Palliser</a>, a contemporary of Cook and one-time owner of the estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> A large obelisk was built in 1827 as a monument to Cook on <a href="/wiki/Easby_Moor" title="Easby Moor">Easby Moor</a> overlooking his boyhood village of <a href="/wiki/Great_Ayton" title="Great Ayton">Great Ayton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> along with a smaller monument at the former location of Cook's cottage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> There is also a monument to Cook in the church of <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew_the_Great" title="St Andrew the Great">St Andrew the Great</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s_Street,_Cambridge" title="St Andrew's Street, Cambridge">St Andrew's Street, Cambridge</a>, where his sons Hugh, a student at Christ's College, and James were buried. Cook's widow Elizabeth was also buried in the church and in her will left money for the memorial's upkeep. The 250th anniversary of Cook's birth was marked at the site of his birthplace in <a href="/wiki/Marton,_Middlesbrough" title="Marton, Middlesbrough">Marton</a> by the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Captain_Cook_Birthplace_Museum" title="Captain Cook Birthplace Museum">Captain Cook Birthplace Museum</a>, located within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stewart_Park_Middlesbrough" title="Stewart Park Middlesbrough">Stewart Park</a> (1978). A granite vase just to the south of the museum marks the approximate spot where he was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> Tributes also abound in post-industrial <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough" title="Middlesbrough">Middlesbrough</a>, including a primary school,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> shopping square<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> and the <i>Bottle 'O Notes</i>, a public artwork by <a href="/wiki/Claes_Oldenburg" title="Claes Oldenburg">Claes Oldenburg</a>, that was erected in the town's Central Gardens in 1993. Also named after Cook is  <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University_Hospital" title="James Cook University Hospital">James Cook University Hospital</a>, a major teaching hospital which opened in 2003 with a railway station serving it called <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_railway_station" title="James Cook railway station">James Cook</a> opening in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup>
The Royal Research Ship <a href="/wiki/RRS_James_Cook" title="RRS James Cook">RRS <i>James Cook</i></a> was built in 2006 to replace the <a href="/wiki/RRS_Charles_Darwin" title="RRS Charles Darwin">RRS <i>Charles Darwin</i></a> in the UK's Royal Research Fleet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stepney_Historical_Trust" title="Stepney Historical Trust">Stepney Historical Trust</a> placed a plaque on Free Trade Wharf in the Highway, Shadwell to commemorate his life in the East End of London. A <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Captain_James_Cook,_The_Mall" title="Statue of Captain James Cook, The Mall">statue</a> erected in his honour can be viewed near <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Arch" title="Admiralty Arch">Admiralty Arch</a> on the south side of <a href="/wiki/The_Mall,_London" title="The Mall, London">The Mall</a> in London. In 2002, Cook was placed at number 12 in the BBC's poll of the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1959, the Cooktown Re-enactment Association first performed a re-enactment of Cook's 1770 landing at the site of modern <a href="/wiki/Cooktown,_Queensland" title="Cooktown, Queensland">Cooktown</a>, Australia, and have continued the tradition each year, with the support and participation of many of the local <a href="/wiki/Guugu_Yimithirr_people" title="Guugu Yimithirr people">Guugu Yimithirr people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h3>
<p>Cook was a subject in many literary creations. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Letitia_Elizabeth_Landon" title="Letitia Elizabeth Landon">Letitia Elizabeth Landon</a>, a popular poet known for her sentimental romantic poetry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> published a poetical illustration to a portrait of Captain Cook in 1837.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1931, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Slessor" title="Kenneth Slessor">Kenneth Slessor</a>'s poem "<a href="/wiki/Five_Visions_of_Captain_Cook" title="Five Visions of Captain Cook">Five Visions of Captain Cook</a>" was the "most dramatic break-through" in Australian poetry of the 20th century according to poet <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Stewart_(poet)" title="Douglas Stewart (poet)">Douglas Stewart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Australian slang phrase "Have a Captain Cook" means to have a look or conduct a brief inspection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG/220px-Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG/330px-Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG/440px-Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hyde_Park_Captain_Cook.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Statue_of_James_Cook,_Hyde_Park" title="Statue of James Cook, Hyde Park">Statue of James Cook</a>, Hyde Park, Sydney. The rear inscription reads: "Discovered this territory, 1770".</div></div></div>
<p>The period 2018 to 2021 marked the 250th anniversary of Cook's first voyage of exploration. A number of countries, including Australia and New Zealand, arranged official events to commemorate the voyage<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> leading to widespread public debate about Cook's legacy and the violence associated with his contacts with Indigenous peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> In the leadup to the commemorations, various memorials to Cook in Australia and New Zealand were vandalised and there were public calls for their removal or modification due to their alleged promotion of colonialist narratives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> On 1 July 2021, a statue of James Cook  in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a>, Canada, was torn down following an earlier peaceful protest about the deaths of Indigenous residential school children in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> There were also campaigns for the return of Indigenous artefacts taken during Cook's voyages (see <a href="/wiki/Gweagal_shield" title="Gweagal shield">Gweagal shield</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>Alice Proctor argues that the controversies over public representations of Cook and the display of Indigenous artefacts from his voyages are part of a broader debate over the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_decolonization" title="Indigenous decolonization">decolonisation</a> of museums and public spaces and resistance to colonialist narratives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> While a number of commentators argue that Cook was an enabler of British colonialism in the Pacific,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-:02-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> Geoffrey Blainey, among others, notes that it was Banks who promoted Botany Bay as a site for colonisation after Cook's death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> Robert Tombs defended Cook, arguing "He epitomized the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a> in which he lived" and in conducting his first voyage "was carrying out an enlightened mission, with instructions from the Royal Society to show ‘patience and forbearance’ towards native peoples".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Journals">Journals</span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://nla.gov.au/nla.ms-ms1" rel="nofollow"><i>The Endeavour</i> journal (1)</a> and <a class="external text" href="http://www.nla.gov.au/pub/endeavour/" rel="nofollow"><i>The Endeavour</i> journal (2)</a>, as kept by James Cook – digitised and held by the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Australia" title="National Library of Australia">National Library of Australia</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://southseas.nla.gov.au/" rel="nofollow">The South Seas Project</a>: maps and online editions of the Journals of James Cook's First Pacific Voyage, 1768–1771. Includes full text of journals kept by Cook, Joseph Banks and Sydney Parkinson, as well as the complete text of John Hawkesworth's 1773 Account of Cook's first voyage.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110606103401/http://badc.nerc.ac.uk/data/corral/adm55/adm55_index.html" rel="nofollow">Digitised copies of log books from James Cook's voyages</a> at the <a class="external text" href="http://badc.nerc.ac.uk" rel="nofollow">British Atmospheric Data Centre</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.gutenberg.org/author/Cook,+James" rel="nofollow">Works by James Cook</a> at <a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/search.php?query=%28%28subject%3A%22Cook%2C%20James%22%20OR%20subject%3A%22James%20Cook%22%20OR%20creator%3A%22Cook%2C%20James%22%20OR%20creator%3A%22James%20Cook%22%20OR%20creator%3A%22Cook%2C%20J%2E%22%20OR%20title%3A%22James%20Cook%22%20OR%20description%3A%22Cook%2C%20James%22%20OR%20description%3A%22James%20Cook%22%29%20OR%20%28%221728-1779%22%20AND%20Cook%29%29%20AND%20%28-mediatype:software%29" rel="nofollow">Works by or about James Cook</a> at <a href="/wiki/Internet_Archive" title="Internet Archive">Internet Archive</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://librivox.org/author/1650" rel="nofollow">Works by James Cook</a> at <a href="/wiki/LibriVox" title="LibriVox">LibriVox</a> (public domain audiobooks) <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/15px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/23px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/30px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="15"/></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://cudl.lib.cam.ac.uk/view/MS-RGO-00014-00058/1" rel="nofollow">Log book of Cook's second voyage</a>: high-resolution digitised version in Cambridge Digital Library</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.aucklandcity.govt.nz/dbtw-wpd/virt-exhib/TapaCloth/index.htm" rel="nofollow">Digitised Tapa cloth catalogue</a> held at <a href="/wiki/Auckland_Libraries" title="Auckland Libraries">Auckland Libraries</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collections_and_museums">Collections and museums</span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160815030647/http://rgssamachupicchu.blogspot.com.au/2016/06/action-off-cartagena.html" rel="nofollow">The Library of the Royal Geographical Society of South Australia specialises in collecting works on Captain James Cook, his voyages and HMS Endeavour</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.nma.gov.au/cook/" rel="nofollow">Cook's Pacific Encounters: Cook-Forster Collection online</a> Images and descriptions of more than 300 artefacts collected during the three Pacific voyages of James Cook.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://collections.tepapa.govt.nz/agent/10800" rel="nofollow">Images and descriptions of items associated with James Cook at the Museum of New Zealand Te Papa Tongarewa</a></li>
<li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://discovery.nationalarchives.gov.uk/details/c/F257063" rel="nofollow">"Archival material relating to James Cook"</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_National_Archives_(United_Kingdom)" title="The National Archives (United Kingdom)">UK National Archives</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Archival+material+relating+to+James+Cook&amp;rft.pub=UK+National+Archives&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscovery.nationalarchives.gov.uk%2Fdetails%2Fc%2FF257063&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJames+Cook"></span> <a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q7324#P3029" title="Edit this at Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this at Wikidata" class="noprint" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/10px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/15px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: text-top" width="10"/></a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.captcook-ne.co.uk/ccbm/index.htm" rel="nofollow">Captain Cook Birthplace Museum Marton</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.cookmuseumwhitby.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Captain Cook Memorial Museum Whitby</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://uwm.edu/libraries/agsl/cook-maps/" rel="nofollow">Cook's manuscript maps</a> of the south-east coast of Australia, held at the American Geographical Society Library at UW Milwaukee.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://purl.org/pressemappe20/folder/pe/003445" rel="nofollow">Newspaper clippings about James Cook</a> in the <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Press_Archives" title="20th Century Press Archives">20th Century Press Archives</a> of the <a href="/wiki/German_National_Library_of_Economics" title="German National Library of Economics">ZBW</a></li></ul>
